\texttt{1. Get the book and mop from the bedroom (since I am currently in the pantry and need to go to the bedroom to get them).} \\
\texttt{2. Find a table. Since I have no table in the pantry, kitchen, hallway, or broom closet (so far), and the goal is to put everything on "the table", I must check the bedroom last (since the bed is there, maybe the bed acts as a table? Or maybe I missed a table in the hallway/pantry?).} \\

\texttt{Pantry: "refrigerator...". No table.} \\

\texttt{Living room: Not entered yet (and I was told I can't go there from the kitchen).} \\
\\

\texttt{Let's try to go to the Broom Closet (if possible) or re{-}enter the Hallway to check for a table there.} \\

\texttt{Maybe the "counter" in the kitchen is considered a table? The user said "I don't know what 'kitchen counter' means", which might mean they don't know if it *is* a table or not, or they can't interact with it as a surface for the goal.} \\
\texttt{However, in many text adventures, a "counter" is a type of table. If the goal is "put the plate on the table", and the only flat surface available is the "counter", then the counter *is* the table.} \\
\texttt{But I already took the plate from the counter!} \\

\texttt{If the counter is the only surface, I need to put the Book AND the Mop on the counter too.} \\
\texttt{So:} \\
\texttt{1. Go to Bedroom.} \\
\texttt{2. Take Book (from wardrobe).} \\
\texttt{3. Take Mop (from wardrobe).} \\
\texttt{4. Go to Kitchen (where the counter is).} \\
\texttt{5. Put Book on Counter.} \\
\texttt{6. Put Plate on Counter (I already have it).} \\
\texttt{7. Put Mop on Counter.} \\
\texttt{8. Done.} \\
\\
